Refrain from Ambiguity, Seek Clarification
Lists rules of conduct for debate including ambiguity and clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to avoid ambiguous language in your own speech and appropriately request clarification when faced with ambiguity in a debate.

Core Idea
In debate, clarity is king; if ambiguity arises, seek clarification before objecting.

The passage begins with a prohibition: 'Refrain from the ambiguous (mujmal).' Why? Because ambiguous statements cause confusion and waste time. However, if such a statement is made, the text permits asking for clarification. This lesson teaches you how to handle ambiguity in a structured debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term 'al-mujmal'
In Islamic jurisprudence and logic, 'mujmal' refers to speech that is not clear in its indication. In a debate, using such speech is prohibited. Look for words that could have multiple meanings or lack context.
Term is stable across usul al-fiqh and mantiq.
2
Recognize the permission of istifsar
The passage states 'wa la ba'sa bil-istifsar' — there is no harm in asking for clarification. This is the proper response when an opponent uses a mujmal expression. Do not assume you understand; ask.
3
Distinguish istifsar from objection
Istifsar is a request for meaning, not a challenge to the claim itself. It should be done respectfully and before any rebuttal.
4
Apply in a sample debate
Imagine a debate about whether a certain act is wajib or mandub. If the opponent says 'The act is obligatory,' but it's unclear which act, you should ask for clarification before proceeding.
Use Islamic fiqh examples only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْمُجْمَلِ (١) ، وَلَا بَأسَ بِالاسْتِفْسَارِ (۲) ، وَعَن الدَّخل (۳) قَبْلَ الفَهم (٤) ، وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالْإِعَادَةِ، وَعَنِ التَّعَرُّضِ لِمَا لَا دَخْلَ لَهُ فِي الْمَقْصُودِ، وَعَنِ الصَّحِكِ وَرَفْعِ الصَّوْتِ وَأَمْثَالِهِمَا (٥)، وَعَنِ الْمُنَاظَرَةِ مَعَ أَهْلِ الْمَهَابَةِ وَالِاحْتِرَامِ (٦) ، وَأَلَّا يَحْسِبَ الْخَصْمَ حقيرًا (۷). هَذَا غَايَةُ مَا يُرَادُ فِي هَذَا الْبَاب وَمِنَ اللهِ التَّوفِيقُ وَإِلْهَامُ الصَّوَاب (۲).
Refrain from the ambiguous (1), and there is no harm in asking for clarification (2), and refrain from entering (3) before understanding (4), and there is no harm in repetition, and refrain from bringing up what has no relevance to the intended purpose, and refrain from laughter and raising the voice and the like (5), and refrain from debating with people of authority and respect (6), and that he should not consider the opponent as lowly (7). This is the utmost of what is desired in this chapter, and from Allah is success and inspiration of correctness.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage enumerates the core etiquettes of debate (adab al-munazara). It begins by prohibiting the use of ambiguous expressions (mujmal), but if such an expression is used, asking for clarification (istifsar) is permissible. Next, it prohibits interrupting the opponent (dakhl) before fully understanding his speech; rather, one must wait until the speaker has finished. Repeating one's point is allowed if needed. Bringing up irrelevant matters (ta'arud) is forbidden. Laughter, loud voices, and similar unbecoming behaviors are prohibited. When debating with a person of authority and respect, one must maintain decorum. Finally, one must never consider the opponent as lowly or insignificant. The passage concludes with a prayer: 'This is the utmost of what is desired in this chapter, and from Allah is success and inspiration of correctness.'

Key Terms
المجمل
الاستفسار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct response when an opponent uses an ambiguous expression (mujmal)?
A) Immediately object to it
B) Ask for clarification (istifsar)
C) Ignore it and continue
D) Consider it a weakness

Key Takeaway
Ambiguity is prohibited in debate, but if it occurs, the proper etiquette is to ask for clarification, not to object prematurely.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a passage from a classical usul text (e.g., al-Shafi'i's Risala) where a mujmal expression appears. Write a dialogue showing how a debater should ask for clarification (istifsar) before responding.
?
In a group discussion, take turns: one person makes an ambiguous claim about a fiqh ruling; the other must ask for clarification using the rules of istifsar.

Dialectic -- Jadal
beginner
5 min
The Prohibition of Interruption and Permission to Repeat
Lists rules of conduct for debate including interruption and repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an interruption (dakhl) occurs and apply the rule of waiting until understanding is complete before responding.

Core Idea
Let the opponent finish before you speak, and you may repeat your point if needed.

The passage prohibits 'al-dakhl qabla al-fahm' — entering into the opponent's speech before understanding. This means interrupting to object or show a flaw before the opponent has fully expressed their argument. However, it permits repetition (al-i'ada) if needed. This lesson focuses on these two related etiquettes.

Guided Path
1
Define 'al-dakhl'
In jadal, al-dakhl is when a respondent cuts off the speaker to raise an objection before the speaker has completed their argument. This is forbidden.
In jadal, specifically means objection before full comprehension.
2
Understand the condition 'qabla al-fahm'
The prohibition is specifically before understanding. If you have understood fully, you may respond, but still politely. The point is to not interrupt prematurely.
3
Note the permission of repetition
'Wa la ba'sa bil-i'ada': Repeating your argument is allowed. This is for clarity, not for stubbornness.
4
Practice in a simulated debate
Have one person speak, and the other tries to interrupt. Reflect on why that is harmful. Then allow repetition.
Use Islamic examples only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'al-dakhl qabla al-fahm' prohibit?
A) Speaking too loudly
B) Interrupting the opponent before fully understanding their speech
C) Asking for clarification
D) Repeating your own argument

Key Takeaway
Do not interrupt your opponent; wait until they finish to ensure full understanding, but feel free to repeat your points for clarity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Write a short dialogue between two students debating whether Madinah-fiqh takes precedence over Basra-fiqh. One student should attempt to interrupt; then rewrite the dialogue following the etiquette.
?
In a pair, one person states an argument from a hadith, and the other must wait until completion before responding. Switch roles and practice the permission to repeat if the response is unclear.
